  </tr>\n         </table>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Washington Metro\n       </b>\n       , known colloquially as\n       <b>\n        Metro\n       </b>\n       and branded\n       <b>\n        Metrorail\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schrag_9_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Schrag_9-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is the heavy rail\n       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">\n        rapid transit\n       </a>\n       system serving the\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">\n        Washington metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       in the United States. It is administered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metropolitan_Area_Transit_Authority" title="Washington Metropolitan Area Transit Authority">\n        Washington Metropolitan Area Transit Authority\n       </a>\n       (WMATA), which also operates\n       <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Metrobus (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Metrobus\n       </a>\n       service under the Metro name.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Besides the District of Columbia, Metro serves several jurisdictions in the states of\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       . In Maryland, Metro provides service to\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Maryland" title="Montgomery County, Maryland">\n        Montgomery\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Prince_George%27s_County,_Maryland" title="Prince George\'s County, Maryland">\n        Prince George\'s\n       </a>\n       counties; in Virginia, to\n       <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">\n        Arlington\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">\n        Fairfax\n       </a>\n       counties and the independent city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">\n        Alexandria\n       </a>\n       . Combined with its ridership in the independent Virginia cities of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falls_Church" title="Falls Church">\n        Falls Church\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fairfax,_Virginia" title="Fairfax, Virginia">\n        Fairfax\n       </a>\n       , the Metro service area is largely coextensive with the inner ring of the Washington metropolitan area. The system is\n       <a href="/wiki/Silver_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Silver Line (Washington Metro)">\n        currently being expanded\n       </a>\n       to reach\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">\n        Dulles International Airport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">\n        Loudoun County, Virginia\n       </a>\n       . It operates mostly as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Passenger_rail_terminology#Subway" title="Passenger rail terminology">\n        subway\n       </a>\n       in the District itself, while most of the suburban tracks are at surface level or\n       <a href="/wiki/Elevated_railway" title="Elevated railway">\n        elevated\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Opened in 1976, the network now includes six lines, 91 stations, and 117 miles (188\xc2\xa0km) of\n       <a href="/wiki/Network_length_(transport)#Route_length" title="Network length (transport)">\n        route\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMATA_History_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WMATA_History-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to subway track depths, Metro\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheaton_station" title="Wheaton station">\n        Wheaton station\n       </a>\n       has the longest, single-tier escalator in the Western Hemisphere, spanning 230 feet (70\xc2\xa0m).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Metro is the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_rapid_transit_systems_by_ridership" title="List of United States rapid transit systems by ridership">\n        third-busiest\n       </a>\n       rapid transit system in the United States in number of passenger trips, after the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">\n        New York City Subway\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chicago_%22L%22" title=\'Chicago "L"\'>\n        Chicago "L"\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APTA-2016-Q4_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-APTA-2016-Q4-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There were 215.3 million trips on Metro in fiscal year 2015, or 712,843 trips per weekday.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmata.com_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmata.com-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In June 2008, Metro set a monthly ridership record with 19,729,641 trips, or 798,456 per weekday.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riders2008_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-riders2008-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Fares vary based on the distance traveled, the time of day, and the type of card used by the passenger. Riders enter and exit the system using a\n       <a href="/wiki/Proximity_card" title="Proximity card">\n        proximity card\n       </a>\n       called\n       <a href="/wiki/SmarTrip" title="SmarTrip">\n        SmarTrip\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2">\n           <a href="#Opening_dates">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Opening dates\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3">\n         <a href="#Architecture">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Architecture\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a href="#System">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Hours_and_headways">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Hours and headways\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11">\n             <a             </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12">\n             <a href="#Rush_Plus">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               3.3.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Rush Plus\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Passenger_information_systems">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Passenger information systems\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">\n         <a href="#Fare_structure">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Fare structure\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Fare_history">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Fare history\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">\n         <a        <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#Security">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Security\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18">\n             <a href="#Random_bag_searches">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.1.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Random bag searches\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Safety">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Safety\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20">\n             <a           </span>\n             </a>\n             <ul>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-21">\n               <a href="#Collisions">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 5.2.1.1\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Collisions\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-22">\n               <a href="#Derailments">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 5.2.1.2\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Derailments\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n             </ul>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23">\n             <a href="#Safety_measures">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               5.2.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Safety measures\n              </span>\n             </a>\n             <ul>\n              <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-24">\n               <a href="#Smoke_incidents">\n                <span class="tocnumber">\n                 5.2.2.1\n                </span>\n                <span class="toctext">\n                 Smoke incidents\n                </span>\n               </a>\n              </li>\n             </ul>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25">\n         <a href="#Future_expansion">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Future expansion\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Silver_Line">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Silver Line\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27">\n           <a href="#Blue_Line_realignment">\n       <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28">\n           <a href="#Orange_Line_extension">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.3\n            </span>\n            <span Meade extensions\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30">\n           <a href="#Potomac_Yard_station">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Potomac Yard station\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31">\n           <a href="#Other_new_rail_lines">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other new rail lines\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32">\n           <a href="#Related_non-WMATA_projects">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Related non-WMATA projects\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36">\n           <a href="#Official_websites">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Official websites\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37">\n           <a href="#Transit_enthusiast_sites">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Transit enthusiast sites\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38">\n           <a href="#Maps">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Maps\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39">\n           <a href="#Equipment">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Equipment\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40">\n           <a href="#Other_websites">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other websites\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DCSubwayConstruction.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="388" data-file-width="625" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/DCSubwayConstruction.jpg/220px-DCSubwayConstruction.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/DCSubwayConstruction.jpg/330px-DCSubwayConstruction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/DCSubwayConstruction.jpg/440px-DCSubwayConstruction.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DCSubwayConstruction.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Metro under construction at the Navy Yard in 1989\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During the 1960s plans were laid for a massive freeway system in Washington.\n       <a href="/wiki/Harland_Bartholomew" title="Harland Bartholomew">\n        Harland Bartholomew\n       </a>\n       , who chaired the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Planning_Commission" title="National Capital Planning Commission">\n        National Capital Planning Commission\n       </a>\n       , thought that a rail transit system would never be self-sufficient because of low density land uses and general transit ridership decline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bartholomew_Contributions_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bartholomew_Contributions-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       But the plan met\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freeway_and_expressway_revolts" title="Freeway and expressway revolts">\n        fierce opposition\n       </a>\n       , and was altered to include a\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">\n        Capital Beltway\n       </a>\n       system plus rail line radials. The Beltway received full funding; funding for the ambitious Inner Loop Freeway system was partially reallocated toward construction of the Metro system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1960 the federal government created the National Capital Transportation Agency to develop a rapid rail system. In 1966, a bill creating WMATA was passed by the federal government, the District of Columbia, Virginia, and Maryland,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMATA_History_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WMATA_History-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with planning power for the system being transferred to it from the NCTA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Building_Metro_-_Planning_pg2_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Building_Metro_-_Planning_pg2-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg">\n         <img alt="Passengers sit in fixed two-seat units. There are metal poles and bars for standees to hold." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg/220px-Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg/330px-Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg/440px-Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dc_metro_car_interior.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Interior of a rehabilitated Breda car\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       WMATA approved plans for a 98-mile (158\xc2\xa0km) regional system in 1968.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Building_Metro_-_Planning_pg2_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Building_Metro_-_Planning_pg2-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Construction began after a groundbreaking ceremony on December 9, 1969, when Secretary of Transportation\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_A._Volpe" title="John A. Volpe">\n        John A. Volpe\n       </a>\n       , District Mayor\n       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Washington" title="Walter Washington">\n        Walter Washington\n       </a>\n       , and Maryland Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Mandel" title="Marvin Mandel">\n        Marvin Mandel\n       </a>\n       tossed the first spade of dirt at Judiciary Square.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first portion of the system opened March 27, 1976, with 4.6 miles (7.4\xc2\xa0km) available on the Red Line with five stations from Rhode Island Avenue to Farragut North, all in the District of Columbia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Arlington County, Virginia was linked to the system on July 1, 1977;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Montgomery County, Maryland, on February 6, 1978;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prince George\'s County, Maryland, on November 20, 1978;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Fairfax County, Virginia, and Alexandria, Virginia, on December 17, 1983.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMATA_History_6-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WMATA_History-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Underground stations were built with cathedral-like arches of concrete, highlighted by soft, indirect lighting.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The name Metro was suggested by\n       <a href="/wiki/Massimo_Vignelli" title="Massimo Vignelli">\n        Massimo Vignelli\n       </a>\n       , who designed the subway maps for the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">\n        New York City Subway\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Martin-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 103-mile (166\xc2\xa0km), 83-station system was completed with the opening of the Green Line segment to Branch Avenue on January 13, 2001. This did not mean the end of the growth of the system: a 3.22-mile (5.18\xc2\xa0km) extension of the Blue Line to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largo_Town_Center_(WMATA_station)" title="Largo Town Center (WMATA station)">\n        Largo Town Center\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morgan_Boulevard_(WMATA_station)" title="Morgan Boulevard (WMATA station)">\n        Morgan Boulevard\n       </a>\n       opened on December 18, 2004. The first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-fill_station" title="In-fill station">\n        in-fill station\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NoMa_%E2%80%93_Gallaudet_University_(WMATA_station)" title="NoMa \xe2\x80\x93 Gallaudet University (WMATA station)">\n        NoMa\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 Gallaudet University\n       </a>\n       (at the time called the New York Ave\xe2\x80\x93Florida Ave\xe2\x80\x93Gallaudet University station) on the Red Line between\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(WMATA_station)" title="Union Station (WMATA station)">\n        Union Station\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Avenue_%E2%80%93_Brentwood_(WMATA_station)" title="Rhode Island Avenue \xe2\x80\x93 Brentwood (WMATA station)">\n        Rhode Island Ave-Brentwood\n       </a>\n       , opened November 20, 2004. Construction began in March 2009 for an extension to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dulles_Airport" title="Dulles Airport">\n        Dulles Airport\n       </a>\n       to be built in two phases.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dulles_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dulles-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first phase, five stations connecting East Falls Church to Tysons Corner and Wiehle Avenue in Reston, opened on July 26, 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Silver_Line_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Silver_Line-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Metro construction required billions of federal dollars, originally provided by Congress under the authority of the National Capital Transportation Act of 1969 (Public Law 91-143). The cost was paid with 67% federal money and 33% local money. This act was amended on January 3, 1980 by Public Law 96-184, "The National Capital Transportation Amendment of 1979" (also known as the Stark-Harris Act), which authorized additional funding of $1.7 billion to permit the completion of 89.5 miles (144.0\xc2\xa0km) of the system as provided under the terms of a full funding grant agreement executed with WMATA in July 1986, which required 20% to be paid from local funds. On November 15, 1990,\n       <a class="external text" href="http://thomas.loc.gov/cgi-bin/query/z?c101:H.R.1463:" rel="nofollow">\n        Public Law 101-551\n       </a>\n       , "The National Capital Transportation Amendments of 1990", authorized an additional $1.3 billion in federal funds for construction of the remaining 13.5 miles (21.7\xc2\xa0km) of the 103-mile (166\xc2\xa0km) system, completed via the execution of full funding grant agreements, with a 63% federal/37% local matching.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The highest ridership for a single day was on the day of the\n       <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama" title="First inauguration of Barack Obama">\n        inauguration of Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       , January 20, 2009, with 1,120,000 riders. It broke the previous record, set the day before, of 866,681 riders.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009_Inauguration_Ridership_Release_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2009_Inauguration_Ridership_Release-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       June 2008 set several ridership records: the single-month ridership record of 19,729,641 total riders, the record for highest average weekday ridership with 1,044,400 weekday trips, had five of the ten highest ridership days, and had 12 weekdays in which ridership exceed 800,000 trips.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riders2008_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-riders2008-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In February 2006 Metro officials chose Randi Miller, a car dealership employee from\n       <a href="/wiki/Woodbridge,_Virginia" title="Woodbridge, Virginia">\n        Woodbridge, Virginia\n       </a>\n       , to record new "doors opening", "doors closing", and "please stand clear of the doors, thank you" announcements after winning an open contest to replace the messages recorded by Sandy Carroll in 1996. The "Doors Closing" contest attracted 1,259 contestants from across the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On October 30, 2010, the crowd at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rally_to_Restore_Sanity_and/or_Fear" title="Rally to Restore Sanity and/or Fear">\n        Rally to Restore Sanity and/or Fear\n       </a>\n       broke a 19-year record in Saturday ridership, with 825,437 trips.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The previous record had been set on June 8, 1991 at 786,358 trips during the Desert Storm rally.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_dates">\n        Opening dates\n       </span>\n <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashburn_(WMATA_station)" title="Ashburn (WMATA station)">\n          Ashburn\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Largo Town Center\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">\n        Architecture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Architecture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Many Metro stations were designed by Chicago architect\n       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Weese" title="Harry Weese">\n        Harry Weese\n       </a>\n       , and are examples of late-20th century\n       <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">\n        modern architecture\n       </a>\n       . With their heavy use of exposed concrete and repetitive design motifs, Metro stations display aspects of\n       <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">\n        Brutalist\n       </a>\n       design. The stations also reflect the influence of Washington\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">\n        neoclassical architecture\n       </a>\n       in their overarching\n       <a href="/wiki/Coffer" title="Coffer">\n        coffered\n       </a>\n       ceiling\n       <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">\n        vaults\n       </a>\n       . Weese worked with\n       <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">\n        Cambridge, Massachusetts\n       </a>\n       -based lighting designer Bill Lam on the indirect lighting used throughout the system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All of Metro\'s original Brutalist stations are found in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Downtown (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Downtown Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       and neighboring urban corridors of\n       <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">\n        Arlington, Virginia\n       </a>\n       , while newer stations incorporate simplified cost-efficient designs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11types_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11types-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2007 the design of the Metro\'s vaulted-ceiling stations was voted number 106 on the "\n       <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Favorite_Architecture" title="America\'s Favorite Architecture">\n        America\'s Favorite Architecture\n       </a>\n       " list compiled by the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Architects" title="American Institute of Architects">\n        American Institute of Architects\n       </a>\n       (AIA), and was the only Brutalist design to win a place among the 150 selected by this public survey.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In January 2014 the AIA announced that it would present its\n       <a href="/wiki/Twenty-five_Year_Award" title="Twenty-five Year Award">\n        Twenty-five Year Award\n       </a>\n       to the Washington Metro system for "an architectural design of enduring significance" that "has stood the test of time by embodying architectural excellence for 25 to 35 years". The announcement cited the key role of Weese, who conceived and implemented a "common design kit-of-parts", which continues to guide the construction of new Metro stations over a quarter-century later, albeit with designs modified slightly for cost reasons.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIA25_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AIA25-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n        <div style="width: 162px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg/240px-WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg/360px-WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg/480px-WMATA_Metro_Center_crossvault_2009.jpg 2x" width="160"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Intersection of\n           <a href="/wiki/Coffer" title="Coffer">\n            coffered\n           </a>\n           concrete\n           <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">\n            ceiling vaults\n           </a>\n           at\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Center_(WMATA_station)" title="Metro Center (WMATA station)">\n            Metro Center\n           </a>\n           (opened 1976), a major transfer station\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 186px">\n        <div style="width: 186px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 184px;">\n          <div srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/12-07-12-wikimania-wdc-by-RalfR-010.jpg/415px-12-07-12-wikimania-wdc-by-RalfR-010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/12-07-12-wikimania-wdc-by-RalfR-010.jpg/553px-12-07-12-wikimania-wdc-by-RalfR-010.jpg 2x" width="184"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           A train departs from\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McPherson_Square_(WMATA_station)" title="McPherson Square (WMATA station)">\n            McPherson Square\n           </a>\n           station (opened 1977), which has an original ceiling vault design\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">\n        <div style="width: 182px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L%27Enfant_Plaza_(WMATA_station).JPG">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/L%27Enfant_Plaza_%28WMATA_station%29.JPG/405px-L%27Enfant_Plaza_%28WMATA_station%29.JPG 1.5x,   </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Canopy over entrance to\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%27Enfant_Plaza_(WMATA_station)" title="L\'Enfant Plaza   <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_Shady_Grove_station.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2100" height="120"        (opened 1984) is a typical original above-ground station\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n        <div style="width: 162px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spring_Hill_Metro_platform_2.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="120"    <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spring_Hill_(WMATA_station)" title="Spring Hill (WMATA station)">\n            Spring Hill\n           </a>\n           (opened 2014) is a typical newer above-ground station\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="System">\n        System\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: System">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Washington_DC_Metro_Map_(To_Scale).svg">\n           <img alt="An actual map with correct distances and geographic placement illustrates how all lines intersect and have many stations in the downtown area, and extend with more widely spaced stations far out into the neighboring areas. This map does not include the Silver Line." data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2025" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Washington_DC_Metro_Map_%28To_Scale%29.svg/300px-Washington_DC_Metro_Map_%28To_Scale%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Washington_DC_Metro_Map_%28To_Scale%29.svg/450px-Washington_DC_Metro_Map_%28To_Scale%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Washington_DC_Metro_Map_%28To_Scale%29.svg/600px-Washington_DC_Metro_Map_%28To_Scale%29.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Map of system drawn to scale. This map does not include the Silver Line.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since opening in 1976, the Metro network has grown to include six lines, 91 stations, and 118 miles (190\xc2\xa0km) of route.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmatafacts_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmatafacts-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The rail network is designed according to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spoke-hub_distribution_paradigm" title="Spoke-hub distribution paradigm">\n        spoke-hub distribution paradigm\n       </a>\n       , with rail lines running between downtown Washington and its nearby suburbs. The system makes extensive use of interlining\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 running more than one service on the same track. There are six operating lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmatafacts_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmatafacts-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The system\'s official map was designed by noted graphic designer\n       <a href="/wiki/Lance_Wyman" title="Lance Wyman">\n        Lance Wyman\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPo_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WaPo-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Bill Cannan while they were partners in the design firm of Wyman &amp; Cannan in New York City.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       About 50 miles (80\xc2\xa0km) of Metro\'s track is underground, as are 47 of the 91 stations. Track runs underground mostly within the District and high-density suburbs. Surface track accounts for about 46 miles (74\xc2\xa0km) of the total, and aerial track makes up 9 miles (14\xc2\xa0km).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmatafacts_34-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmatafacts-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The system operates on a unique\n       <a href="/wiki/Track_gauge" title="Track gauge">\n        track gauge\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_rolling_stock" title="Washington Metro rolling stock">\n        <span class="nowrap">\n         4\xc2\xa0ft\n         <span class="frac">\n          8\n          <span class="visualhide">\n          </span>\n          <sup>\n           1\n          </sup>\n          \xe2\x81\x84\n          <sub>\n           4\n          </sub>\n         </span>\n         in\n        </span>\n       </a>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        1,429\xc2\xa0mm\n       </span>\n       ). This is 1/4 of an inch narrower than\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        4\xc2\xa0ft\n        <span class="frac">\n         8\n         <span class="visualhide">\n         </span>\n         <sup>\n          1\n         </sup>\n         \xe2\x81\x84\n         <sub>\n          2\n         </sub>\n        </span>\n        in\n       </span>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        1,435\xc2\xa0mm\n       </span>\n       )\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">\n         standard gauge\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="(December 2016)">\n           why?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In an effort to gain revenues, WMATA has started to allow retail ventures in Metro stations. WMATA has authorized DVD-rental vending machines and ticket booths for the Old Town Trolley Tours and is seeking additional retail tenants.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin: 0 auto; text-align:left;">\n       <caption style="margin:inherit; class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largo_Town_Center_Station" title="Largo Town Center Station">\n          Largo Town Center\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Financing">\n        Financing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Financing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Metro relies extensively on passenger fares and appropriated financing from the Maryland, Virginia, and Washington D.C. governments, which are represented on Metro\'s board of directors. The system does not have a dedicated revenue stream as other cities\' mass transit systems do. Critics allege that this has contributed to Metro\'s recent history of maintenance and safety problems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For Fiscal Year 2015, the estimated\n       <a href="/wiki/Farebox_recovery_ratio" title="Farebox recovery ratio">\n        farebox recovery ratio\n       </a>\n       (fare revenue divided by operating expenses) was 66 percent, based on the WMATA approved budget.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">\n        Infrastructure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stations">\n        Stations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Stations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Washington_Metro_stations" title="List of Washington Metro stations">\n        List of Washington Metro stations\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There are 40 stations in the District of Columbia, 15 in Prince George\'s County, 11 in Montgomery County, 11 in Arlington County, 11 in Fairfax County, and three in the City of Alexandria.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmatafacts_34-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmatafacts-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The second phase of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Silver_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Silver Line (Washington Metro)">\n        Silver Line\n       </a>\n       will add 6 new stations\xe2\x80\x94three more in Fairfax County and three in\n       <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">\n        Loudoun County, Virginia\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94in 2019 or 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 196 feet (60\xc2\xa0m) below the surface, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forest_Glen_(WMATA_station)" title="Forest Glen (WMATA station)">\n        Forest Glen\n       </a>\n       station on the Red Line is the deepest in the system. There are no escalators; high-speed elevators take 20 seconds to travel from the street to the station platform. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wheaton_(WMATA_station)" title="Wheaton (WMATA station)">\n        Wheaton\n       </a>\n       station, one stop to the north of the Forest Glen station, has the longest continuous escalator in the USA and in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">\n        Western Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       , at 230 feet (70\xc2\xa0m).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmatafacts_34-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmatafacts-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosslyn_(WMATA_station)" title="Rosslyn (WMATA station)">\n        Rosslyn\n       </a>\n       station is the deepest station on the Orange/Blue Line, at 117 feet (36\xc2\xa0m) below street level. The station features the second-longest continuous escalator in the Metro system at 194 feet (59\xc2\xa0m); an escalator ride between the street level and the mezzanine level takes nearly two minutes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The system is not centered on any single station, but\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Center_(WMATA_station)" title="Metro Center (WMATA station)">\n        Metro Center\n       </a>\n       is at the intersection of the Red, Orange, Blue, and Silver Lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2008guide_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2008guide-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The station is also the location of WMATA\'s main sales office. Metro has designated five other "core stations" that have high passenger volume, including:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corestations_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-corestations-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallery_Place_(WMATA_station)" title="Gallery Place (WMATA station)">\n        Gallery Place\n       </a>\n       , transfer station for the Red, Green and Yellow Lines;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%27Enfant_Plaza_(WMATA_station)" title="L\'Enfant Plaza (WMATA station)">\n        L\'Enfant Plaza\n       </a>\n       , transfer station for the Orange, Blue, Silver, Green and Yellow Lines;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(WMATA_station)" title="Union Station (WMATA station)">\n        Union Station\n       </a>\n       , the busiest station by passenger boardings;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2008guide_43-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2008guide-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farragut_North_(WMATA_station)" title="Farragut North (WMATA station)">\n        Farragut North\n       </a>\n       ; and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farragut_West_(WMATA_station)" title="Farragut West (WMATA station)">\n        Farragut West\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In order to deal with the high number of passengers in transfer stations, Metro is studying the possibility of building pedestrian connections between nearby core transfer stations. For example, a 750-foot (230\xc2\xa0m) passage between Metro Center and Gallery Place stations would allow passengers to transfer between the Orange/Blue/Silver and Yellow/Green Lines without going one stop on the Red Line. Another tunnel between Farragut West and Farragut North stations would allow transfers between the Red and Orange/Blue/Silver lines, decreasing transfer demand at Metro Center by an estimated 11%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corestations_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-corestations-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Farragut pedestrian tunnel has yet to be physically implemented, but was added in virtual form effective October 28, 2011. The SmarTrip system now interprets an exit from one Farragut station and entrance to the other as part of a single trip, allowing card holders to transfer on foot without having to pay a second full fare.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">\n        Rolling stock\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_rolling_stock" title="Washington Metro rolling stock">\n        Washington Metro rolling stock\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rohr_train.jpg">\n         <img alt="An exterior perspective view of a train, with its distinct brown and metallic design, at a station platform." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Rohr_train.jpg/220px-Rohr_train.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Rohr_train.jpg/330px-Rohr_train.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Rohr_train.jpg/440px-Rohr_train.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rohr_train.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Train of Rohr cars arriving at the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheverly_(WMATA_station)" title="Cheverly (WMATA station)">\n          Cheverly station\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Metro\xe2\x80\x99s fleet consists of 1,126 rail cars, each 75 feet (22.86\xc2\xa0m) long.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sunnov08_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sunnov08-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Trains have a maximum speed of 75\xc2\xa0mph (121\xc2\xa0km/h), and average 33\xc2\xa0mph (53\xc2\xa0km/h), including stops. Operating rules presently limit their top speed to 59\xc2\xa0mph (95\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmatafacts_34-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmatafacts-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All cars operate as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Married_pair" title="Married pair">\n        married pairs\n       </a>\n       (consecutively numbered even-odd with a cab at each end of the pair except 7000 series railcars), with systems shared across the pair.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro currently operates 850 cars during rush hours. There are 814 cars in active service, four cars have been permanently removed from revenue service for use as the "\n       <a href="/wiki/Money_train" title="Money train">\n        money train\n       </a>\n       ", and the remaining 36 cars compose gap trains to serve as backup should a train experience problems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:center">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Series\n      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metro_Press_Release_50-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Metro_Press_Release-50">\n           [50]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metro_Press_Release_50-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Metro_Press_Release-50">\n           [50]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         7000 series\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_rolling_stock#5000-series" title="Washington Metro rolling stock">\n          5000\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         CAF / AAI\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         194\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2001\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2019 \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         192\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         7000 series\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_rolling_stock#6000-series" title="Washington Metro rolling stock">\n          6000\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Alstom\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         184\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2005\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         184\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n id="cite_ref-Metro_Press_Release_50-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Metro_Press_Release-50">\n           [50]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_rolling_stock#8000-series" title="Washington Metro rolling stock">\n          8000\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         (not selected)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         366\n         <br/>\n         (expected)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2023\n         <br/>\n         (expected)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       NOTE: Retirement dates are estimates for the 2000, 3000, and 5000 series trains.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 5000 series CAF trains are expected to be retired in 2019 because of poor quality and unreliability.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Metro\'s rolling stock was acquired in six phases, and each version of car is identified with a separate series number. The original order of 300 rail cars (90 of which are in operation as of April 18, 2017\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) was manufactured by\n       <a href="/wiki/Rohr,_Inc." title="Rohr, Inc.">\n        Rohr Industries\n       </a>\n       , with final delivery in 1978. These cars are numbered 1000\xe2\x80\x931299 and were rehabilitated in the mid-1990s.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breda_Costruzioni_Ferroviarie" title="Breda Costruzioni Ferroviarie">\n        Breda Costruzioni Ferroviarie\n       </a>\n       (Breda), now\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AnsaldoBreda" title="AnsaldoBreda">\n        AnsaldoBreda\n       </a>\n       , manufactured the second order of 76 cars delivered in 1983 and 1984. These cars, numbered 2000\xe2\x80\x932075, were rehabilitated in the early 2000s by\n       <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">\n        Alstom\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hornell,_New_York" title="Hornell, New York">\n        Hornell, New York\n       </a>\n       . A third order of 288 cars, also from Breda, were delivered between 1984 and 1988. These cars are numbered 3000\xe2\x80\x933291 and were rehabilitated by Alstom in the early 2000s. An order of 100 cars from Breda, numbered 4000\xe2\x80\x934099, were delivered between 1992 and 1994. A fifth order of 192 cars was manufactured by\n       <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_y_Auxiliar_de_Ferrocarriles" title="Construcciones y Auxiliar de Ferrocarriles">\n        Construcciones y Auxiliar de Ferrocarriles\n       </a>\n       (CAF) of Spain. These cars are numbered 5000\xe2\x80\x935191 and were delivered from 2001 through 2004. A sixth order of 184 cars from Alstom Transportation, are numbered 6000-6183 and were delivered between 2005 and 2007. The cars have body shells built in\n       <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">\n        Barcelona, Spain\n       </a>\n       with assembly completed in Hornell, New York.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-currentcars_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-currentcars-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 7000 series of cars, currently being built by\n       <a href="/wiki/Kawasaki_Heavy_Industries_Rolling_Stock_Company" title="Kawasaki Heavy Industries Rolling Stock Company">\n        Kawasaki Heavy Industries Rolling Stock Company\n       </a>\n       of Kobe, Japan are being delivered for on-site testing during winter 2013, and first entered service April 14, 2015 on the Blue Line. The new cars are different from previous models in that while still operating as married pairs, the cab in one car was eliminated, turning it into a B car. The new design allows for increased passenger capacity, elimination of redundant equipment, greater energy efficiency, and lower maintenance costs. The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Transportation_Safety_Board" title="National Transportation Safety Board">\n        National Transportation Safety Board\n       </a>\n       investigation of the fatal June 22, 2009, accident led it to conclude that the 1000 series cars are unsafe and unable to protect passengers in a crash. As a result, on July 26, 2010, Metro voted to purchase 300 7000 series cars to replace the remaining 1000 series cars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An additional 128 7000 series cars were also ordered to serve the new Silver Line to Dulles Airport (64 for each phase). In May 2013, Metro placed another order for 100 7000 series cars, which will replace all of the 4000 series cars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On July 13, 2015, WMATA used their final option and purchased an additional 220 7000 series railcars for fleet expansion, bringing the total number of 7000 series railcars on order to 748.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Signaling_and_operation">\n        Signaling and operation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Signaling and operation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_signaling_and_operation" title="Washington Metro signaling and operation">\n        Washington Metro signaling and operation\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During normal passenger operation on revenue tracks, trains are designed to be controlled by an integrated\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_Train_Operation" title="Automatic Train Operation">\n        Automatic Train Operation\n       </a>\n       (ATO) and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_Train_Control" title="Automatic Train Control">\n        Automatic Train Control\n       </a>\n       (ATC) system that accelerates and brakes trains automatically without operator intervention. All trains are still manned with train operators who open and close the doors, make station announcements, and supervise their trains. The system was designed so that an operator could manually operate a train when necessary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since June 2009, when\n       <a href="/wiki/June_2009_Washington_Metro_train_collision" title="June 2009 Washington Metro train collision">\n        two Red Line trains collided\n       </a>\n       and killed nine people due in part to malfunctions in the ATC system, all Metro trains have been manually operated.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manual_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Manual-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The current state of manual operation has led to heavily degraded service, with new manual requirements such as absolute blocks, speed restrictions, and end-of-platform stopping leading to increased headways between trains, increased dwell time, and worse on-time performance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro originally planned to have all trains be automated again by 2017,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but those plans were shelved in early 2017 in order to focus on more pressing safety and infrastructure issues.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The train doors were originally designed to be opened and closed automatically and the doors would re-open if an object blocked them, much as elevator doors do. Almost immediately after the system opened in 1976 Metro realized these features were not conducive to safe or efficient operation and they were disabled. At present the doors may be opened automatically or manually. If a door tries to close and it meets an obstruction, the operator must re-open the door.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hours_and_headways">\n        Hours and headways\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hours and headways">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Metrorail begins service at 5 am Monday through Friday, 7 am on Saturdays, and 8 am Sundays; it ends service at 11:30 pm Monday through Thursday, 1:00 am Friday and Saturday, and 11:00 pm on Sundays, although the last trains leave the end stations inbound about half an hour before these times.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n          <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (February 2017)">\n           not in citation given\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Trains run more frequently during rush hours on all lines, with scheduled peak hour headways of 4 minutes on the Red Line and 9 minutes on all other lines. Headways are much longer during midday and evening on weekdays and all weekend. The midday six-minute headways are based on a combination of two Metrorail lines (Orange/Blue and Yellow/Green) as each route can run every 12 minutes; in the case of the Red Line, every other train bound for Glenmont terminates at Silver Spring instead. Night and weekend service varies between 8 and 24 minutes, with trains generally scheduled only every 20 minutes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other service truncations also occur in the system during rush hour service only. On the Red Line, every other train bound for Shady Grove terminates at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grosvenor%E2%80%93Strathmore_(WMATA_station)" title="Grosvenor\xe2\x80\x93Strathmore (WMATA station)">\n        Grosvenor-Strathmore\n       </a>\n       , in addition to the alternating terminations at Silver Spring mentioned above. For the Yellow Line, all trains bound for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Totten_(WMATA_station)" title="Fort Totten (WMATA station)">\n        Fort Totten\n       </a>\n       terminate at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon_Square_(WMATA_station)" title="Mount Vernon Square (WMATA station)">\n        Mount Vernon Square\n       </a>\n       . These are primarily instituted due to a limited supply of rail cars and the locations of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pocket_track" title="Pocket track">\n        pocket tracks\n       </a>\n       throughout the system.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Until 1999, Metro ended service at midnight every night, and weekend service began at 8 am. That year, WMATA began late night service on Fridays and Saturdays until 1 am. By 2007, with encouragement from businesses, that closing time had been pushed back to 3 am,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with peak fares in effect for entries after midnight. There were plans floated to end late night service due to costs in 2011, but they were met with resistance by riders.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       WMATA temporarily discontinued late night rail service on May 30, 2016, so that Metro can conduct an extensive track rehabilitation program in an effort to improve the system\'s reliability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On June 25, 2017, Metro changed its hours of operation with closing at 11:30 PM Monday\xe2\x80\x93Thursday, 1 AM on Friday and Saturday, and 11 PM on Sunday,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-june25_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-june25-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with the last trains leaving the end stations inbound about half an hour before these times.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Special_service_patterns">\n        Special service patterns\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Special service patterns">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Metro runs special service patterns on holidays and when events in Washington may require additional service.\n       <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">\n        Independence Day\n       </a>\n       activities require Metro to adjust service to provide extra capacity to and from the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Mall" title="National Mall">\n        National Mall\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       WMATA makes similar adjustments during other events, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_inauguration" title="United States presidential inauguration">\n        presidential inaugurations\n       </a>\n       . Metro has altered service and used some stations as entrances or exits only to help manage congestion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rush_Plus">\n        Rush Plus\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rush Plus">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       In 2012, WMATA announced enhanced rush period service that was implemented on June 18, 2012, under the name \xe2\x80\x9cRush+\xe2\x80\x9d (or \xe2\x80\x9cRush Plus\xe2\x80\x9d). Rush Plus service occurred only during portions of peak service: 6:30\xe2\x80\x939:00 AM and 3:30\xe2\x80\x936:00 PM, Monday through Friday.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Rush+ realignment was intended to free up space in the Rosslyn Portal (the tunnel between Rosslyn and Foggy Bottom), which operates at full capacity already. When Silver Line service began, those trains would be routed through the tunnel, and so some of what were Blue Line trains to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largo_Town_Center_(WMATA_station)" title="Largo Town Center (WMATA station)">\n        Largo Town Center\n       </a>\n       were now diverted across the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/14th_Street_Bridge_(Potomac_River)" title="14th Street Bridge (Potomac River)">\n        Fenwick Bridge\n       </a>\n       to become Yellow Line trains running all the way up the Green Line to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenbelt_(WMATA_station)" title="Greenbelt (WMATA station)">\n        Greenbelt\n       </a>\n       . Select Yellow Line trains running south diverted along the Blue Line to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franconia-Springfield_(WMATA_station)" title="Franconia-Springfield (WMATA station)">\n        Franconia-Springfield\n       </a>\n       (as opposed to the normal Yellow line terminus at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huntington_(WMATA_station)" title="Huntington (WMATA station)">\n        Huntington\n       </a>\n       ). Until the start of Silver Line service, excess Rosslyn Tunnel capacity was used by additional Orange Line trains that traveled along the Blue Line to Largo (as opposed to the normal Orange Line terminus at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Carrollton_(WMATA_station)" title="New Carrollton (WMATA station)">\n        New Carrollton\n       </a>\n       ). Rush+ had the additional effect of giving some further number of passengers transfer-free journeys, though severely increasing headways for the portion of the Blue Line running between\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentagon_(WMATA_station)" title="Pentagon (WMATA station)">\n        Pentagon\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosslyn_(WMATA_station)" title="Rosslyn (WMATA station)">\n        Rosslyn\n       </a>\n       . In May 2017, Metro announced that Yellow Rush+ service would be eliminated effective June 25, 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_information_systems">\n        Passenger information systems\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Passenger information systems">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28,_2010.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28%2C_2010.jpg/220px-Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28%2C_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28%2C_2010.jpg/330px-Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28%2C_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28%2C_2010.jpg/440px-Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28%2C_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gallery_Pl-Chinatown_Upper_Level_January_28,_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         PIDS signs at the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallery_Place_(WMATA_station)" title="Gallery Place (WMATA station)">\n          Gallery Place station\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Passenger_information_system" title="Passenger information system">\n        Passenger Information Display System\n       </a>\n       (PIDS) was installed in all Metrorail stations in 2000. Displays are located on all track platforms and at the mezzanine entrances of stations, and provide real-time information on next train arrivals, delayed trains, emergency announcements, and related information.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       WMATA also provides current train and related information to customers with conventional\n       <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">\n        web browsers\n       </a>\n       , as well as users of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smartphones" title="Smartphones">\n        smartphones\n       </a>\n       and other mobile devices.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2010 Metro began sharing its PIDS data with outside software developers, for use in creating additional real-time applications for mobile devices. Free apps are available to the public on major mobile device software platforms (\n       <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">\n        iOS\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">\n        Android\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">\n        Windows Phone\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Palm_(PDA)" title="Palm (PDA)">\n        Palm\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       WMATA also began providing real-time train information by phone in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n
