</sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fare_structure">\n        Fare structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Fare structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/SmarTrip" title="SmarTrip">\n        SmarTrip\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg">\n         <img alt="A row of fare-card machines, each with buttons, slots for money and farecards, and printed instructions." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1192" data-file-width="1700" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg/220px-WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg/330px-WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg/440px-WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_farecard_vending_machines.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Standard self-service vending machines for passes and farecards located at each station\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Riders enter and exit the system using a\n       <a href="/wiki/Stored-value_card" title="Stored-value card">\n        stored-value card\n       </a>\n       in the form of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Proximity_card" title="Proximity card">\n        proximity card\n       </a>\n       known as\n       <a href="/wiki/SmarTrip" title="SmarTrip">\n        SmarTrip\n       </a>\n       . The fare is deducted from the balance of the card when exiting.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SmarTrip cards can be purchased at station vending machines, online or at retail outlets, and can store up to $300 in value.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Metro fares vary based on the distance traveled and the time of day at entry. During peak hours (weekdays from opening until 9:30\xc2\xa0a.m. and 3\xe2\x80\x937\xc2\xa0p.m.), fares (effective 2014) range from $2.25 to $6.00, depending on distance traveled. At all other times, fares range from $2.00 to $3.85 based on distance traveled. Discounted fares are available for school children, the disabled, and the elderly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fares_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fares-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro charges reduced fares on all\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_holidays_in_the_United_States" title="Federal holidays in the United States">\n        federal holidays\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n          <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2017)">\n           not in citation given\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since June 25, 2017, the first fare hike in three years, peak-period rail fares increased 10 cents, with $2.25 as the new minimum and $6 as the maximum one-way fare. Off-peak fares rose 25 cents, to $2 minimum, $3.85 maximum, as will bus fares.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-june25_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-june25-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A new one-day unlimited rail\n       <span class="Unicode nowrap">\n       </span>\n       /\n       <span class="Unicode nowrap">\n       </span>\n       bus pass will be available for $14.75.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-june25_67-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-june25-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Passengers may purchase passes at farecard vending machines. Passes are loaded onto the same SmarTrip cards as stored value, but grant riders unlimited travel within the system for a certain period of time. The period of validity starts with the first use. Four types of passes are currently sold:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        A One Day Pass for $14.75, valid for one day of unlimited Metrorail travel. The pass expires at the end of the operating day.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A 7-Day Short Trip Pass for $38.50, valid for seven consecutive days for Metrorail trips costing up to $3.85 (the maximum off-peak fare) during peak fare times and any trip during off-peak hours. If the trip costs more than $3.60 the difference is deducted from the cash balance of a SmarTrip card, possibly after the necessary value is added at the Exitfare machine. A non-negative stored value is required to enter the Metrorail system.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n         <a href="#cite_note-85">\n          [85]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A 7-Day Fast Pass for $60.00, valid for seven consecutive days of unlimited Metrorail travel.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n         <a href="#cite_note-86">\n          [86]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A 28-Day Metrorail Fast Pass for $237. This is for convenience only, offering no savings over four uses of the 7-Day Fast Pass.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       In addition, Metro sells SelectPass, available for purchase online only by registered SmarTrip cardholders, valid for trips up to a specified value for a specific calendar month, with the balance being deducted from the card\xe2\x80\x99s cash value similarly to the Short Trip Pass.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The pass is priced based on 18 days of round-trip travel.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SelectPass is available in the following values:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:0 0 15px 20px; text-align:center">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Trip value\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Rail-Only\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Rail+Bus\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $2.25\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n         </span>\n         $81.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $126.00\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x80\xa1\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $2.50\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n         </span>\n         $90.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $2.75\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="nowrap">\n         </span>\n         $99.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $3.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $108.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $3.25\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $117.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $3.50\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $126.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $3.75\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $135.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $180.00\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x80\xa1\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         $4.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         $144.00\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <span style="visibility:hidden">\n          <sup>\n           \xe2\x80\xa1\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         $5.90\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x80\xa1\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span style="visibility:hidden">\n          <sup>\n           \xe2\x80\xa1\n          </sup>\n         </span>\n         $212.40\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x80\xa1\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         N/A\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="3">\n         <sup>\n          \xe2\x80\xa1\n         </sup>\n         <small>\n          Beginning on June 16, pricing for the Rail+Bus SelectPass and the maximum fare\n          <br/>\n          SelectPass for the month of July will be increased to reflect the June 25 fare changes.\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Users can add value to any farecard. Riders pay an\n       <a href="/wiki/Exit_fare" title="Exit fare">\n        exit fare\n       </a>\n       based on time of day and distance traveled. Trips may include segments on multiple lines under one fare as long as the rider does not exit the faregates, with the exception of the "Farragut Crossing" out-of-station interchange between\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farragut_West" title="Farragut West">\n        Farragut West\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farragut_North" title="Farragut North">\n        Farragut North\n       </a>\n       stations. At Farragut Crossing, riders may exit from one station and reenter at the other within 30 minutes on a single fare. When making a trip that uses Metrobus and Metrorail, a 50\xc2\xa2 discount is available when using a SmarTrip card.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bus_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bus-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When entering and exiting at the same station, users are normally charged a minimum fare ($2.15 / $1.75). However since July 1, 2016 users have had a 15 minute grace period to exit the station; those who do so will receive a rebate of the amount paid as an autoload to their SmarTrip card.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Students at District of Columbia public schools ride both Metrobus and Metrorail for free.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fare_history">\n        Fare history\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fare history">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Farecardfront.jpg">\n         <img alt="Metro farecard has a column of printed dollar amounts, a magnetic strip along the edge, and in this example a drawing of two pandas." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="276" data-file-width="170" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/87/Farecardfront.jpg" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Farecardfront.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Front face of an old paper Metro farecard, listing declining-balance value remaining\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The contract for Metro\'s fare collection system was awarded in 1975 to\n       <a href="/wiki/Cubic_Transportation_Systems" title="Cubic Transportation Systems">\n        Cubic Transportation Systems\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cts.cubic.com_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cts.cubic.com-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Electronic fare collection using paper\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_stripe" title="Magnetic stripe">\n        magnetic stripe\n       </a>\n       cards started on July 1, 1977, a little more than a year after the first stations opened. Prior to electronic fare collection, exact change fareboxes were used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro\'s historic paper farecard system is also shared by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BART#Fares" title="BART">\n        Bay Area Rapid Transit\n       </a>\n       , which Cubic won a contract for in 1974.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cts.cubic.com_95-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cts.cubic.com-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Any remaining value stored on the paper cards was printed on the card at each exit, and passes were printed with the expiration date.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Several adjustments were made to shift the availability of passes from paper tickets to SmarTrip cards in 2012 and 2013. In May 2014 Metro announced plans to retrofit more than 500 fare vending machines throughout the system to dispense SmarTrip cards, rather than paper fare cards, and eventually eliminate magnetic fare cards entirely.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was completed in early December 2015 when the last paper farecard was sold.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The faregates stopped accepting paper farecards on March 6, 2016,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paperless_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-paperless-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the last day for trading in farecards to transfer the value to SmarTrip was June 30, 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paperless_100-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-paperless-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_and_security">\n        Safety and security\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Safety and security">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Security">\n        Security\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Security">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Metro_Transit_Police_Department" title="Metro Transit Police Department">\n        Metro Transit Police Department\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg/220px-Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg/330px-Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg/440px-Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Metro_Transit_Police_Department_cruiser.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Metro Transit Police cruiser\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Metro planners designed the system with passenger safety and order maintenance as primary considerations. The open vaulted ceiling design of stations and the limited obstructions on platforms allow few opportunities to conceal criminal activity. Station platforms are built away from station walls to limit vandalism and provide for diffused lighting of the station from recessed lights. Metro\'s attempts to reduce crime, combined with how the station environments were designed with\n       <a href="/wiki/Crime_prevention_through_environmental_design" title="Crime prevention through environmental design">\n        crime prevention\n       </a>\n       in mind,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lavigne_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lavigne-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       has contributed to Metro being among the safest and cleanest subway systems in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lavigne2_102-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lavigne2-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are nearly 6,000 video surveillance cameras used across the system to enhance security.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Metro is patrolled by its own police force, which is charged with ensuring the safety of passengers and employees. Transit Police officers patrol the Metro system and\n       <a href="/wiki/Metrobus_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Metrobus (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Metrobuses\n       </a>\n       , and they have jurisdiction and arrest powers throughout the 1,500-square-mile (3,900\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) Metro service area for crimes that occur on or against transit authority facilities, or within 150 feet (46\xc2\xa0m) of a Metrobus stop. The Metro Transit Police Department is one of two U.S. police agencies that has local police authority in three "state"-level jurisdictions (Maryland, Virginia, and the District of Columbia), the U.S. Park Police being the other.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metro_Police_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Metro_Police-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Each city and county in the Metro service area has similar ordinances that regulate or prohibit vending on Metro-owned property, and which prohibit riders from eating, drinking, or smoking in Metro trains, buses, and stations; the Transit Police have a reputation for enforcing these laws rigorously. One widely publicized incident occurred in October 2000 when police arrested 12-year-old Ansche Hedgepeth for eating\n       <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">\n        french fries\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenleytown%E2%80%93AU_(WMATA_station)" title="Tenleytown\xe2\x80\x93AU (WMATA station)">\n        Tenleytown-AU\n       </a>\n       station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In a 2004 opinion by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_G._Roberts" title="John G. Roberts">\n        John Roberts\n       </a>\n       , now\n       <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">\n        Chief Justice of the United States\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D.C._Circuit_Court_of_Appeals" title="D.C. Circuit Court of Appeals">\n        D.C. Circuit Court of Appeals\n       </a>\n       upheld Hedgepeth\'s arrest.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hedgepeth_case_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hedgepeth_case-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By then WMATA had answered negative publicity by adopting a policy of first issuing warnings to\n       <a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">\n        juveniles\n       </a>\n       , and arresting them only after three violations within a year.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Metro\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zero-tolerance" title="Zero-tolerance">\n        zero-tolerance\n       </a>\n       policy on food, trash and other sources of disorder embodies the "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broken_windows" title="Broken windows">\n        broken windows\n       </a>\n       " philosophy of crime reduction. This philosophy also extends to the use of station restroom facilities. A longstanding policy, intended to curb unlawful and unwanted activity, has been to only allow employees to use Metro restrooms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lavigne2_102-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lavigne2-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Station managers may make exceptions for passengers with small children, the elderly, or the disabled.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Layton_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Layton-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro now allows the use of restrooms by passengers who gain a station manager\'s permission, except during periods of heightened\n       <a href="/wiki/Homeland_Security_Advisory_System" title="Homeland Security Advisory System">\n        terror alerts\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Random_bag_searches">\n        Random bag searches\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Random bag searches">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On October 27, 2008, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Metro_Transit_Police_Department" title="Metro Transit Police Department">\n        Metro Transit Police Department\n       </a>\n       announced plans to immediately begin random searches of backpacks, purses, and other bags. Transit police would search riders at random before boarding a bus or entering a station. It also explained its intent to stop anyone acting suspiciously.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro claims that the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Second_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit">\n        United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit\n       </a>\n       decision in\n       <i>\n        MacWade v. Kelly\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which upheld random searches on the New York City Subway, allows Metro Transit Police to take similar action.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metro Transit Police Chief Michael Taborn stated that, if someone were to turn around and simply enter the system through another escalator or elevator, Metro has "a plan to address suspicious behavior".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Security expert\n       <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Schneier" title="Bruce Schneier">\n        Bruce Schneier\n       </a>\n       characterized the plan as "\n       <a href="/wiki/Security_theater" title="Security theater">\n        security theater\n       </a>\n       against a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie_plot_threat" title="Movie plot threat">\n        movie plot threat\n       </a>\n       " and does not believe random bag searches actually improve security.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Metro Riders\' Advisory Council recommended to WMATA\xe2\x80\x99s board of directors that Metro hold at least one public meeting regarding the search program. As of December 2008\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , Metro had not conducted a single bag search.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2010 Metro once again announced that it would implement random bag searches, and conducted the first such searches on December 21, 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The searches consist of swabbing bags and packages for explosive residue, and\n       <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">\n        X-raying\n       </a>\n       or opening any packages which turned up positive. On the first day of searches, at least one false positive for explosives was produced, which Metro officials indicated could occur for a variety of reasons including if a passenger had recently been in contact with firearms or been to a firing range.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The D.C. Bill of Rights Coalition and the Montgomery County Civil Rights Coalition circulated a petition against random bag searches, taking the position that the practice violates the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution">\n        Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution\n       </a>\n       and would not improve security.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On January 3, 2011, Metro held a public forum for the searches at a Metro Riders\' Advisory Council meeting, at which more than 50 riders spoke out, most of them in opposition to the searches. However at the meeting Metro officials called random bag inspections a "success" and claimed that few riders had complained.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After a prolonged absence, as of February 2017\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , bag searches have resumed at random stations throughout the Washington Metro area.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">\n        Safety\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Safety">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">\n        Accidents and incidents\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Incidents_on_the_Washington_Metro" title="Incidents on the Washington Metro">\n        Incidents on the Washington Metro\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Several collisions have occurred on Washington Metro, resulting in injuries and fatalities, along with numerous derailments with few or no injuries. WMATA has been criticized for disregarding safety warnings and advice from experts. The Tri-State Oversight Committee oversaw WMATA, but had no regulatory authority. Metro\'s safety department is usually in charge of investigating incidents, but could not require other Metro departments to implement its recommendations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-safetywarnings_119-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-safetywarnings-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Following several safety lapses, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Transit_Administration" title="Federal Transit Administration">\n        Federal Transit Administration\n       </a>\n       assumed oversight at WMATA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Collisions">\n        Collisions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Collisions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png">\n         <img alt="A badly damaged subway car sticks up at an angle where it had partially ridden over another car in an underground station." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="438" data-file-width="719" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png/220px-NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png/330px-NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png/440px-NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NTSB-Woodley-Park-Accident.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Crash at the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodley_Park_(WMATA_station)" title="Woodley Park (WMATA station)">\n          Woodley Park station\n         </a>\n         on November 3, 2004\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blizzard_of_1996" title="Blizzard of 1996">\n        Blizzard of 1996\n       </a>\n       , on January 6, a Metro operator was killed when a train failed to stop at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shady_Grove_(WMATA_station)" title="Shady Grove (WMATA station)">\n        Shady Grove\n       </a>\n       station. The four-car train overran the station platform and struck an unoccupied train that was awaiting assignment. The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Transportation_Safety_Board" title="National Transportation Safety Board">\n        National Transportation Safety Board\n       </a>\n       (NTSB) investigation found that the crash was a result of a failure in the train\'s computer-controlled braking system. The NTSB recommended that Metro grant train operators the ability to manually control the braking system, even in inclement weather, and recommended that Metro prohibit parked rail cars on tracks used by incoming outbound trains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On November 3, 2004, an out-of-service Red Line train rolled backwards into the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodley_Park_(WMATA_station)" title="Woodley Park (WMATA station)">\n        Woodley Park\n       </a>\n       station, hitting an in-service train stopped at the platform. The rear car (1077) was\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telescoping_(railway)" title="Telescoping (railway)">\n        telescoped\n       </a>\n       by the first car of the standing train (4018). No one was killed, but 20 people were injured.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 14-month investigation concluded that the train operator was most likely not alert as the train rolled backwards into the station. Safety officials estimated that had the train been full, at least 79 people would have died. The train operator was dismissed and Metro officials agreed to add rollback protection to more than 300 rail cars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:June_22,_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="1419" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/June_22%2C_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg/220px-June_22%2C_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/June_22%2C_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg/330px-June_22%2C_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/June_22%2C_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg/440px-June_22%2C_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:June_22,_2009_WMATA_Collision_-_NTSB_accident_photo_422860.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/June_2009_Washington_Metro_train_collision" title="June 2009 Washington Metro train collision">\n          June 22, 2009 crash\n         </a>\n         , in which nine people were killed.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On June 22, 2009, at 5:02\xc2\xa0pm,\n       <a href="/wiki/June_2009_Washington_Metro_train_collision" title="June 2009 Washington Metro train collision">\n        two trains on the Red Line collided\n       </a>\n       . A southbound train heading toward Shady Grove stopped on the track short of the Fort Totten station and another southbound train collided with its rear. The front car of the moving train (1079) was telescoped by the rear car of the standing train (5066),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTSB_Fort_Totten_Abstract_124-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NTSB_Fort_Totten_Abstract-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and passengers were trapped. Nine people died and more than 70 were injured, dozens of whom were described as "\n       <a href="/wiki/Walking_wounded" title="Walking wounded">\n        walking wounded\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Red Line service was suspended between the Fort Totten and Takoma stations, and New Hampshire Avenue was closed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of the dead was the operator of the train that collided with the stopped train.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On November 29, 2009, at 4:27\xc2\xa0am,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/November_29,_2009_Washington_Metro_train_collision" title="November 29, 2009 Washington Metro train collision">\n        two trains collided\n       </a>\n       at the West Falls Church train yard. One train pulled in and collided into the back of the other train. No customers were aboard, and only minor injuries to the operators and cleaning staff were reported. However, three cars (1106, 1171, and 3216) were believed to be damaged beyond repair.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yardcollision_128-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-yardcollision-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Derailments">\n        Derailments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Derailments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg">\n         <img alt="The crushed end of a subway car." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg/220px-WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg/330px-WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg/440px-WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WMATA_CAF_5152_derailment.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Green Line train following the January 7, 2007 derailment\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On January 13, 1982, a train\n       <a href="/wiki/1982_Washington_Metro_train_derailment" title="1982 Washington Metro train derailment">\n        derailed\n       </a>\n       at a malfunctioning crossover switch south of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Triangle_(WMATA_station)" title="Federal Triangle (WMATA station)">\n        Federal Triangle\n       </a>\n       station. In attempting to restore the train to the rails, supervisors failed to notice that another car had also derailed. The other rail car slid off the track and hit a tunnel support, killing three people and injuring 25. Coincidentally, this crash occurred about 30 minutes after\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_Florida_Flight_90" title="Air Florida Flight 90">\n        Air Florida Flight 90\n       </a>\n       crashed into the nearby\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/14th_Street_Bridge_(Potomac_River)" title="14th Street Bridge (Potomac River)">\n        14th Street Bridge\n       </a>\n       during a major snowstorm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMATA_History_6-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WMATA_History-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On January 20, 2003, during construction of a new canopy at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Airport_(WMATA_station)" title="National Airport (WMATA station)">\n        National Airport\n       </a>\n       station, Metro began running trains through the center track even though it had not been constructed for standard operations, and a Blue Line train derailed at the switch. No injuries resulted but the crash delayed construction by a number of weeks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-February_27.2C_2003_129-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-February_27.2C_2003-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On January 7, 2007, a Green Line train carrying approximately 120 people derailed near the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Vernon_Square_(WMATA_station)" title="Mount Vernon Square (WMATA station)">\n        Mount Vernon Square\n       </a>\n       station in downtown Washington. Trains were single-tracking at the time, and the derailment of the fifth car occurred where the train was switching from the south to northbound track. The crash injured at least 18 people and prompted the rescue of 60 people from a tunnel.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At least one person had a serious but non-life-threatening injury.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan07_131-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jan07-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Mount Vernon Square crash was one of a series of five derailments involving\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Metro_rolling_stock#5000-Series" title="Washington Metro rolling stock">\n        5000-Series\n       </a>\n       cars, with four of those occurring on side tracks and not involving passengers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jan07_131-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jan07-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On June 9, 2008, an Orange Line train (2000-series) derailed between the Rosslyn and Court House stations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On February 12, 2010, a Red Line train derailed at about 10:13\xc2\xa0am as it left the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farragut_North_(WMATA_station)" title="Farragut North (WMATA station)">\n        Farragut North\n       </a>\n       station in downtown Washington. After leaving the station, the train entered the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pocket_track" title="Pocket track">\n        pocket track\n       </a>\n       north of the station. As it continued, an\n       <a href="/wiki/Derail" title="Derail">\n        automatic derailer\n       </a>\n       at the end of the pocket track intentionally derailed the train as a safety measure. If the train had continued moving forward on the pocket track, it would have entered the path of an oncoming train. The wheels of the first two cars in the six-car, White-Flint-bound train were forced off the tracks, stopping the train. Almost all of the estimated 345 passengers were evacuated from the damaged train by 11:50\xc2\xa0am and the NTSB arrived on the scene by noon. Two minor injuries were reported, and a third passenger was taken to\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_University_Hospital" title="George Washington University Hospital">\n        George Washington University Hospital\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The NTSB ruled the crash was due to the train operator\'s failure to follow standard procedures and WMATA management for failure to provide proper supervision of the train operator which resulted in the incomplete configuration of the train identification and destination codes leading to the routing of the train into the pocket track.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On April 24, 2012, around 7:15 pm, a Blue Line train bound for Franconia\xe2\x80\x93Springfield derailed near Rosslyn. No injuries were reported.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On July 6, 2012, around 4:45 pm, a Green Line train bound for downtown Washington, D.C. and Branch Avenue derailed near West Hyattsville. No injuries were reported. A\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heat_kink" title="Heat kink">\n        heat kink\n       </a>\n       , due to the hot weather, was identified as the probable cause of the accident.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On August 6, 2015, a non-passenger train derailed outside Smithsonian station. The track condition that caused the derailment had been detected a month earlier but was not repaired.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On July 29, 2016, a Silver Line train heading in the direction of Wiehle-Reston East station derailed outside East Falls Church station. Service was suspended between Ballston and West Falls Church and McLean stations on the Orange and Silver Lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On September 1, 2016, Metro announced the derailment of an empty six-car train in the Alexandria Rail Yard. No injuries or service interruptions were reported and an investigation is ongoing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">\n        <a href="#cite_note-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_measures">\n        Safety measures\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Safety measures">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On July 13, 2009, WMATA adopted a "zero tolerance" policy for train or bus operators found to be texting or using other hand-held devices while on the job. This new and stricter policy came after investigations of several mass-transit accidents in the U.S. found that operators were texting at the time of the accident. The policy change was announced the day after a passenger of a Metro train videotaped the operator texting while operating the train.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">\n        <a href="#cite_note-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h5>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Smoke_incidents">\n        Smoke incidents\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Smoke incidents">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h5>\n      <p>\n       On January 12, 2015, during early evening rush, a Yellow Line train stopped in the tunnel and filled with smoke just after departing L\'Enfant Plaza for Pentagon due to "an electrical arcing event" ahead in the tunnel. Everyone on board was evacuated; 84 people were taken to hospitals and one person died.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On March 14, 2016, an electrified rail caught fire between McPherson Square and Farragut West, causing significant disruptions on the Blue, Orange, and Silver lines. On March 15, a decision was made to close the entire rail network the following day to inspect the network\'s entire electric rail power grid.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansion">\n        Future expansion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Future expansion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       WMATA expects an average of one million riders daily by 2030. The need to increase capacity has renewed plans to add 220 cars to the system and reroute trains to alleviate congestion at the busiest stations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Population growth in the region has also revived efforts to extend service, build new stations, and construct additional lines.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Silver_Line">\n        Silver Line\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Silver Line">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1750" data-file-width="3551" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG/300px-VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG/450px-VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG/600px-VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VA_07_2012_Tysons_Central_123_Metro_Station_3639.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The new\n         <a href="/wiki/Tysons_Corner_station" title="Tysons Corner station">\n          Tysons Corner station\n         </a>\n         under construction next to\n         <a href="/wiki/Virginia_State_Route_123" title="Virginia State Route 123">\n          Virginia State Route 123\n         </a>\n         in July 2012\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Silver_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Silver Line (Washington Metro)">\n        Silver Line (Washington Metro)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The most prominent expansion is the Dulles Corridor Metrorail Project, dubbed the Silver Line, a 23-mile (37\xc2\xa0km) extension from the Orange Line into\n       <a href="/wiki/Loudoun_County,_Virginia" title="Loudoun County, Virginia">\n        Loudoun County, Virginia\n       </a>\n       , by way of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tysons_Corner,_Virginia" title="Tysons Corner, Virginia">\n        Tysons Corner\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">\n        Washington Dulles International Airport\n       </a>\n       . Rail to Dulles has been discussed since the system opened in 1976. The current Silver Line project was formally proposed in 2002 and initially approved by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Transit_Administration" title="Federal Transit Administration">\n        Federal Transit Administration\n       </a>\n       in 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silverfact_145-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-silverfact-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After several delays, federal funding for Phase 1 was secured in December 2008\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and construction began in March 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timeline_147-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-timeline-147">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The line is being constructed in two phases; the first phase to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiehle_%E2%80%93_Reston_East_(WMATA_station)" title="Wiehle \xe2\x80\x93 Reston East (WMATA station)">\n        Wiehle \xe2\x80\x93 Reston East\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Reston,_Virginia" title="Reston, Virginia">\n        Reston, Virginia\n       </a>\n       opened July 26, 2014,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n        <a href="#cite_note-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the second phase to\n       <a href="/wiki/Ashburn_station_(Washington_Metro)" title="Ashburn station (Washington Metro)">\n        Ashburn\n       </a>\n       , beyond Dulles Airport, is projected for completion in 2019 or 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsletter-nov-2012_149-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-newsletter-nov-2012-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Blue_Line_realignment">\n        Blue Line realignment\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Blue Line realignment">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Blue Line trains share a single tunnel with Orange Line and Silver Line trains to cross the Potomac River. The current tunnel limits service in each direction, creating a choke point. A 2001 proposal would have rerouted the Blue Line between the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosslyn_(WMATA_station)" title="Rosslyn (WMATA station)">\n        Rosslyn\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadium%E2%80%93Armory_(WMATA_station)" title="Stadium\xe2\x80\x93Armory (WMATA station)">\n        Stadium\xe2\x80\x93Armory\n       </a>\n       stations by building a bridge or tunnel from Virginia to a new station in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Washington,_D.C." title="Georgetown, Washington, D.C.">\n        Georgetown\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NARPAC_150-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NARPAC-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The proposal was later rejected due to cost,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but Metro again started considering a similar scenario in 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weir-14June2011_152-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Weir-14June2011-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orange_Line_extension">\n        Orange Line extension\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Orange Line extension">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Virginia Department of Transportation (VDOT) announced on January 18, 2008, that it and the Virginia Department of Rail and Public Transportation (DRPT) had begun work on a draft environmental impact statement (EIS) for the I-66 corridor in Fairfax and Prince William counties. According to VDOT the EIS, officially named the I-66 Multimodal Transportation and Environment Study, would focus on improving mobility along I-66 from the Capital Beltway (I-495) interchange in Fairfax County to the interchange with U.S. Route 15 in Prince William County. The EIS also allegedly includes a four-station extension of the Orange Line past Vienna. The extension would continue to run in the I-66 median and would have stations at Chain Bridge Road, Fair Oaks, Stringfellow Road and Centreville near Virginia Route 28 and U.S. Route 29.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In its final report published June 8, 2012, the study and analysis revealed that an "extension would have a minimal impact on Metrorail ridership and volumes on study area roadways inside the Beltway and would therefore not relieve congestion in the study corridor."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fort_Belvoir_and_Fort_Meade_extensions">\n        Fort Belvoir and Fort Meade extensions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Fort Belvoir and Fort Meade extensions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 2005 the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        Defense Department\n       </a>\n       announced that it would be shifting 18,000 jobs to\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Belvoir" title="Fort Belvoir">\n        Fort Belvoir\n       </a>\n       in Virginia and at least 5,000 jobs to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Meade" title="Fort Meade">\n        Fort Meade\n       </a>\n       in Maryland by 2012, as part of that year\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_Base_Realignment_and_Closure_Commission" title="2005 Base Realignment and Closure Commission">\n        Base Realignment and Closure\n       </a>\n       plan. In anticipation of such a move, local officials and the military proposed extending the Blue and Green Lines to service each base. The proposed extension of the Green Line could cost $100 million per mile ($60 million per kilometer), and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">\n        light rail\n       </a>\n       extension to Fort Belvoir was estimated to cost up to $800 million. Neither proposal has established timelines for planning or construction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-belvoir_155-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-belvoir-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meade_156-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-meade-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Potomac_Yard_station">\n        Potomac Yard station\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Potomac Yard station">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Yard_station" title="Potomac Yard station">\n        Potomac Yard station\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2008 officials began to explore the possibility of adding an\n       <a href="/wiki/Infill_station" title="Infill station">\n        infill station\n       </a>\n       called\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Yard_station" title="Potomac Yard station">\n        Potomac Yard\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Yard" title="Potomac Yard">\n        Potomac Yard\n       </a>\n       area of Alexandria, on the Blue and Yellow Lines between the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport_(WMATA_station)" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport (WMATA station)">\n        National Airport\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Braddock_Road_station" title="Braddock Road station">\n        Braddock Road\n       </a>\n       stations. In 2010 the Alexandria City Council approved a portion of the proposed $240 million construction of the station. Construction would start in 2017 and the station is expected to open in 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-board_157-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-board-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_new_rail_lines">\n        Other new rail lines\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Other new rail lines">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 2011 Metro began studying the needs of the system through 2040.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weir-14June2011_152-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Weir-14June2011-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New Metro rail lines and extensions under consideration as part of this long term plan include: a new line which parallels the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_Beltway" title="Capital Beltway">\n        Capital Beltway\n       </a>\n       ; a new line from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Friendship_Heights_(WMATA_station)" title="Friendship Heights (WMATA station)">\n        Friendship Heights\n       </a>\n       Metro station to\n       <a href="/wiki/White_Oak,_Maryland" title="White Oak, Maryland">\n        White Oak, Maryland\n       </a>\n       , which would pass through the District and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silver_Spring_(WMATA_station)" title="Silver Spring (WMATA station)">\n        Silver Spring\n       </a>\n       ; an extension of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Green Line (Washington Metro)">\n        Green Line\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Harbor" title="National Harbor">\n        National Harbor\n       </a>\n       in Maryland; and re-routing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Blue Line (Washington Metro)">\n        Blue Line\n       </a>\n       in the District between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orange_Line_(Washington_Metro)" title="Orange Line (Washington Metro)">\n        Orange Line\n       </a>\n       and Green Line. None of these lines are yet funded for planning or construction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weir-14June2011_152-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Weir-14June2011-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Related_non-WMATA_projects">\n        Related non-WMATA projects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Related non-WMATA projects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Washington_Purple_Line.png">\n         <img alt="A scaled map illustrating the Purple Line route and its intersections with existing subway lines." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="835" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Washington_Purple_Line.png/300px-Washington_Purple_Line.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Washington_Purple_Line.png/450px-Washington_Purple_Line.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Washington_Purple_Line.png/600px-Washington_Purple_Line.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Washington_Purple_Line.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Proposed route of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Purple_Line_(Maryland)" title="Purple Line (Maryland)">\n          Purple Line\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">\n        light rail\n       </a>\n       and urban\n       <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">\n        streetcar\n       </a>\n       projects have been proposed to extend or supplement service provided by Metro. Like the Silver Line in Virginia, the proposed\n       <a href="/wiki/Purple_Line_(Maryland)" title="Purple Line (Maryland)">\n        Purple Line\n       </a>\n       has been in planning since the 1980s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shaver_158-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-shaver-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The project was originally envisioned as a circular heavy rail line connecting the outer stations on each branch of the Metrorail system, in a pattern roughly mirroring the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_495_(Capital_Beltway)" title="Interstate 495 (Capital Beltway)">\n        Capital Beltway\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The current proposal would create a light rail system in Maryland between the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bethesda_(WMATA_station)" title="Bethesda (WMATA station)">\n        Bethesda\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Carrollton_(WMATA_station)" title="New Carrollton (WMATA station)">\n        New Carrollton\n       </a>\n       stations by way of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silver_Spring_(WMATA_station)" title="Silver Spring (WMATA station)">\n        Silver Spring\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_Park_%E2%80%93_University_of_Maryland_(WMATA_station)" title="College Park \xe2\x80\x93 University of Maryland (WMATA station)">\n        College Park\n       </a>\n       . Such a plan would connect both branches of the Red Line to the Green and Orange Lines, and would decrease the travel time between suburban Metro stations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shaver_158-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-shaver-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">\n        <a href="#cite_note-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Corridor_Cities_Transitway" title="Corridor Cities Transitway">\n        Corridor Cities Transitway\n       </a>\n       (CCT) is a proposed 15-mile (24\xc2\xa0km)\n       <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">\n        bus rapid transit\n       </a>\n       line that would link\n       <a href="/wiki/Clarksburg,_Maryland" title="Clarksburg, Maryland">\n        Clarksburg, Maryland\n       </a>\n       in northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Maryland" title="Montgomery County, Maryland">\n        Montgomery County\n       </a>\n       with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shady_Grove_(WMATA_station)" title="Shady Grove (WMATA station)">\n        Shady Grove\n       </a>\n       station on the Red Line.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoCo_Planning_161-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MoCo_Planning-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Assuming that the anticipated federal, state, and local government funds are provided, construction of the first 9 miles (14\xc2\xa0km) of the system would begin in 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2005, a Maryland lawmaker proposed a light rail system to connect areas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Maryland" title="Southern Maryland">\n        Southern Maryland\n       </a>\n       , especially the rapidly growing area around the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Waldorf,_Maryland" title="Waldorf, Maryland">\n        Waldorf\n       </a>\n       , to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branch_Avenue_(WMATA_station)" title="Branch Avenue (WMATA station)">\n        Branch Avenue\n       </a>\n       station on the Green Line.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">\n        <a href="#cite_note-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The District of Columbia Department of Transportation is building the new\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D.C._Streetcar" title="D.C. Streetcar">\n        D.C. Streetcar\n       </a>\n       system to improve transit connectivity within the District. A tram line to connect\n       <a href="/wiki/Bolling_Air_Force_Base" title="Bolling Air Force Base">\n        Bolling Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anacostia_(WMATA_station)" title="Anacostia (WMATA station)">\n        Anacostia\n       </a>\n       station and was originally expected to open in 2010. Streetcar routes have been proposed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlas_District" title="Atlas District">\n        Atlas District\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capitol_Hill,_Washington,_D.C." title="Capitol Hill, Washington, D.C.">\n        Capitol Hill\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/K_Street_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="K Street (Washington, D.C.)">\n        K Street corridor\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">\n        <a href="#cite_note-164">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After seven years of construction, the Atlas District route, known as the H/Benning Street route, opened on February 27, 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">\n        <a href="#cite_note-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2013, the Georgetown Business Improvement District proposed a\n       <a href="/wiki/Gondola_lift" title="Gondola lift">\n        gondola lift\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Georgetown (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Georgetown\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Rosslyn,_Virginia" title="Rosslyn, Virginia">\n        Rosslyn\n       </a>\n       as an alternative to placing a Metro stop at Georgetown in its 2013\xe2\x80\x932028 economic plans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dcgondola1_166-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dcgondola1-166">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Washington, D.C and Arlington County have been conducting feasibility studies for it since 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dcgondola1_166-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dcgondola1-166">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Metro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a ridership\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Transportation in Washington, D.C.">\n         Transportation in Washington, D.C.\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol_Subway_System" title="United States Capitol Subway System">\n         United States
